# Issue 20592: relocate-once.py does not handle local/bin/gp-2.8

I'm using the binary distribution of sage 7.1 (64 bit) on Ubuntu 14.04: http://mirrors.mit.edu/sage/linux/64bit/sage-7.1-Ubuntu_14.04-x86_64.tar.bz2

It seems that the `relocate-once.py` script does not rewrite the path of `local/bin/gp-2.8` causing:

```
$ sage -gp
gp: error while loading shared libraries: libpari-gmp-2.8.so.0: cannot open shared object file: No such file or directory
```

```
$ ldd libpari-gmp-2.8.so.0
linux-vdso.so.1 => (0x00007fff480b7000)
libc.so.6 => /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libc.so.6 (0x00007f8cc3ec1000)
libm.so.6 => /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libm.so.6 (0x00007f8cc3bbb000)
libgmp.so.16 => /lmfdb/SageMath/local/lib/libgmp.so.16 (0x00007f8cc392b000)
libdl.so.2 => /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libdl.so.2 (0x00007f8cc3727000)
/lib64/ld-linux-x86-64.so.2 (0x000055aa62509000)
```

**CC:**  @vbraun

**Reviewer:** Jeroen Demeyer

Issue created by migration from https://trac.sagemath.org/ticket/20592

<a id='comment:2'></a>
Actually a better report should be to give us the output of `ldd -r local/bin/gp` because it is `gp` that is failing to load `libpari-gmp-2.8.so.0`. I'd like the output of `readelf -d /lmfdb/SageMath/local/bin/gp` as well. Also I notice you say

```
# sage -gp
```
and not

```
# ./sage -gp
```
Is the root of your sage install (`/lmfdb/SageMath`) in your `PATH`? If you somehow call `sage` from the wrong install install I can foresee problems.

<a id='comment:3'></a>
Sorry for the delay.

So I downloaded the binary from http://mirrors.mit.edu/sage/linux/64bit/sage-7.1-Ubuntu_14.04-x86_64.tar.bz2, unpacked it and then started it as written before (and it was surely the correct runtime as there was no other sage version installed on this VM on GCE).

Here are the outputs:

<a id='comment:8'></a>
No, it doesn't. It works after reinstalling pari manually but it does not work out of the box with the provided binary.
The reason is obviously given by

```
   SageMath$ ldd -r local/bin/gp
        linux-vdso.so.1 =>  (0x00007ffc6199e000)
        libpari-gmp-2.8.so.0 => not found [...]
```
even though the file is there.

All the outputs are from a fresh install.

```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:11'></a>\nI can confirm the same problem with the sage-7.2-Fedora_23-x86_64.tar.bz2 tarball. Conspicuously, `bin/gphelp` does occur in the `patching ...` lines, but `bin/gp` does not. Same as what Ehlen reports. So wherever the files-to-be-patched are listed, `bin/gp` does not seem to be in that list.\n\nIndeed, in the file `relocate-once.py` the file `local/bin/gp` is not mentioned, and `local/bin/python2.7` is. I don't know where the fix needs to be made, but what the effect of the fix should be is pretty clear.\n\n**EDIT:** It would seem this line: [binary-package/package.py:244](https://github.com/sagemath/binary-pkg/blob/c4622f83e130edb0ddc229d27c4fb027dc86abe2/binary_pkg/package.py#L244) doesn't get executed for `local/bin/gp`. Clearly, the executable does get staged, so it would seem that the string matching heuristics somehow miss the path reference in `local/bin/gp`. Hopefully Volker will be able to see what goes wrong here.",
    "created_at": "2016-05-17T23:14:50Z",
```

<a id='comment:11'></a>
I can confirm the same problem with the sage-7.2-Fedora_23-x86_64.tar.bz2 tarball. Conspicuously, `bin/gphelp` does occur in the `patching ...` lines, but `bin/gp` does not. Same as what Ehlen reports. So wherever the files-to-be-patched are listed, `bin/gp` does not seem to be in that list.

Indeed, in the file `relocate-once.py` the file `local/bin/gp` is not mentioned, and `local/bin/python2.7` is. I don't know where the fix needs to be made, but what the effect of the fix should be is pretty clear.

**EDIT:** It would seem this line: [binary-package/package.py:244](https://github.com/sagemath/binary-pkg/blob/c4622f83e130edb0ddc229d27c4fb027dc86abe2/binary_pkg/package.py#L244) doesn't get executed for `local/bin/gp`. Clearly, the executable does get staged, so it would seem that the string matching heuristics somehow miss the path reference in `local/bin/gp`. Hopefully Volker will be able to see what goes wrong here.

archive/issue_comments_300215.json:
```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:20'></a>\nReplying to [vbraun](#comment%3A18):\n> I'm aware of that. The binary-pkg script does not patch the gp binary because it has some unclear text/binary end-of-string markers. It also prints a warning while packing. Sage doesn't need the gp binary, though.\n\n\nIf we have to we could deprecate `sage -gp` (but that would be a shame). However, removing `sage.interfaces.gp` is not an option. Currently, `modular.buzzard`, `lfunctions.dokchitser`, schemes.elliptic_curves.gp_simon` depend on it. The scenarios there create a separate instance of a `gp` interpreter (for good reason!), so I don't think we'll be rewriting those very soon to work with the pari library directly.\n\nSo, in order to ensure the current binary packaging strategy is viable, I think we need to clarify the unclear text/binary end-of-string markers in the gp executable.",

```

<a id='comment:20'></a>
Replying to [vbraun](#comment%3A18):
> I'm aware of that. The binary-pkg script does not patch the gp binary because it has some unclear text/binary end-of-string markers. It also prints a warning while packing. Sage doesn't need the gp binary, though.


If we have to we could deprecate `sage -gp` (but that would be a shame). However, removing `sage.interfaces.gp` is not an option. Currently, `modular.buzzard`, `lfunctions.dokchitser`, schemes.elliptic_curves.gp_simon` depend on it. The scenarios there create a separate instance of a `gp` interpreter (for good reason!), so I don't think we'll be rewriting those very soon to work with the pari library directly.

So, in order to ensure the current binary packaging strategy is viable, I think we need to clarify the unclear text/binary end-of-string markers in the gp executable.



---

archive/issue_comments_300216.json:
```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:21'></a>\nI've looked in the GP binary and the to-be-replaced path occurs 3 times in the file: (writing \\0 for a zero byte. All other characters around it are ascii):\n\n```\n\\0__bss_start\\0/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/usr/lib\\0rectcolor\\0\n```\nso the to-be-replaced string occurs several times in what seems to be a 0-terminated string. Can't we just:\n- scan for the pattern\n- get the shortest 0-terminated block that contains the pattern\n- verify that this block looks like an ascii string\n- do a search-and-replace on the string\n- check that the new string isn't longer than what it was before\n- pad the new string with 0-bytes so that it has the right length, and make this the new block\n- overwrite the old block with the new block\nI checked on the GP binary, and executing the recipe above on it (well, I used a hex editor for this one-off operation) leads to a functioning executable. We're making a bit of an assumption that padding with 0 is an allowable thing to do. Apparently it is in the case of the gp executable. If it's too risky in general, perhaps only allow this recipe on whitelisted files (and whitelist the gp executable)?",
    "created_at": "2016-05-19T07:52:19Z",
    "issue": "https://github.com/sagemath/sagetest/issues/20592",
    "type": "issue_comment",
    "url": "https://github.com/sagemath/sagetest/issues/20592#issuecomment-300216",
    "user": "https://github.com/nbruin"
}
```

<a id='comment:21'></a>
I've looked in the GP binary and the to-be-replaced path occurs 3 times in the file: (writing \0 for a zero byte. All other characters around it are ascii):

```
\0__bss_start\0/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/mnt/disk/home/buildslave-sage/slave/binary_pkg/build/source/SageMath/jc4b6yulaujayb9sr94ia88eourzeq/local/lib:/usr/lib\0rectcolor\0
```
so the to-be-replaced string occurs several times in what seems to be a 0-terminated string. Can't we just:
- scan for the pattern
- get the shortest 0-terminated block that contains the pattern
- verify that this block looks like an ascii string
- do a search-and-replace on the string
- check that the new string isn't longer than what it was before
- pad the new string with 0-bytes so that it has the right length, and make this the new block
- overwrite the old block with the new block
I checked on the GP binary, and executing the recipe above on it (well, I used a hex editor for this one-off operation) leads to a functioning executable. We're making a bit of an assumption that padding with 0 is an allowable thing to do. Apparently it is in the case of the gp executable. If it's too risky in general, perhaps only allow this recipe on whitelisted files (and whitelist the gp executable)?



---
